<td style="border:0; padding:0; vertical-align:middle; text-align:right;"><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Slavonia,_Baranja_and_Western_Syrmia_(1995%E2%80%9398)" title="Eastern Slavonia, Baranja and Western Syrmia (1995–98)">Eastern Slavonia, Baranja and Western Syrmia (1995–98)</a></td>
<td style="border:0; padding:0; vertical-align:middle;"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="281" data-file-width="562" height="10" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_Eastern_Slavonia_-_Baranja_-_and_Western_Syrmia.svg/20px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_Eastern_Slavonia_-_Baranja_-_and_Western_Syrmia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_Eastern_Slavonia_-_Baranja_-_and_Western_Syrmia.svg/30px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_Eastern_Slavonia_-_Baranja_-_and_Western_Syrmia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_Eastern_Slavonia_-_Baranja_-_and_Western_Syrmia.svg/40px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_Eastern_Slavonia_-_Baranja_-_and_Western_Syrmia.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></td>

<tr>
<td colspan="2"><b>Today part of</b></td>
<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Croatia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Croatia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Croatia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Croatia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Croatia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Croatia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="3"><small>Area source: <big><span style="position: relative; top: 0.5em;"><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-klajn_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-klajn-3">[3]</a></sup></span></big><br/>
Population source: <big><span style="position: relative; top: 0.5em;"><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-klajn_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-klajn-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-svarm_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-svarm-4">[4]</a></sup></span></big></small></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>Republic of Serbian Krajina</b> (<b>RSK</b>; <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>: <span lang="sr" xml:lang="sr">Република Српска Крајина (РСК) / <i>Republika Srpska Krajina</i></span>, <small>pronounced </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Serbo-Croatian" title="Help:IPA for Serbo-Croatian">[rɛpǔblika sr̩̂pskaː krâjina]</a></span>; sometimes translated as <b>Republic of Serb Krajina</b>), commonly known as <b>Serbian Krajina</b> or simply <b>Krajina</b>, was a self-proclaimed <a href="/wiki/Serbs_of_Croatia" title="Serbs of Croatia">Serb</a> parastate<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hicvs_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-hicvs-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indeks_oluja_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-indeks_oluja-6">[6]</a></sup> within the territory of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Croatia" title="Republic of Croatia">Republic of Croatia</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Croatian_War_of_Independence" title="Croatian War of Independence">Croatian War of Independence</a>. Established in 1991, it was not recognized internationally. It formally existed from 1991 to 1995, having been initiated a year earlier via smaller separatist regions. The name <i><a href="/wiki/Krajina" title="Krajina">Krajina</a></i> ("Frontier") was adopted from the historical borderland, the <a href="/wiki/Military_Frontier" title="Military Frontier">Military Frontier</a>, of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Empire" title="Austro-Hungarian Empire">Austro-Hungarian Empire</a>, which existed up to the 19th century. Its <a href="/wiki/Separatism" title="Separatism">separatist</a> government engaged in a war for ethnic Serb independence from the Republic of Croatia, within and out of <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>, once Croatian borders had been recognized by foreign states in August 1991 and February 1992.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Milan_Babi%C4%87" title="Milan Babić">Milan Babić</a>, former President of Serbian Krajina, testified to the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_former_Yugoslavia" title="International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia">International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia</a> (ICTY) that Krajina was provided with weapons by <a href="/wiki/Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Slobodan Milošević">Slobodan Milošević</a>'s government in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Serbia_(1990%E2%80%932006)" title="Republic of Serbia (1990–2006)">Serbia</a>, and that Krajina was economically and financially dependent upon Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Babic testified that Milošević held <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> control over both the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Serbian_Krajina" title="Military of Serbian Krajina">Army of Serbian Krajina</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_People%27s_Army" title="Yugoslav People's Army">Yugoslav People's Army</a> (JNA) during its actions in Krajina via an alternate chain of command through the Serbian police.</p>
<p>The government of Krajina had <i>de facto</i> control over central parts of the territory while control of the outskirts changed with the successes and failures of its military activities. The territory was legally protected by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Protection_Force" title="United Nations Protection Force">United Nations Protection Force</a> (UNPROFOR).</p>
<p>Its main portion was overrun by Croatian forces in 1995 and the Republic of Serbian Krajina was ultimately disbanded as a result; a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Slavonia,_Baranja_and_Western_Syrmia_(1995-1998)" title="Eastern Slavonia, Baranja and Western Syrmia (1995-1998)">rump remained in eastern Slavonia</a> under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Transitional_Authority_for_Eastern_Slavonia,_Baranja_and_Western_Sirmium" title="United Nations Transitional Authority for Eastern Slavonia, Baranja and Western Sirmium">UNTAES</a> administration until its peaceful reintegration into Croatia in 1998.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_Serbian_Krajina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_Serbian_Krajina&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small><i>(August 2014)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The name <i><a href="/wiki/Krajina" title="Krajina">Krajina</a></i> (meaning "frontier") stemmed from the <a href="/wiki/Military_Frontier" title="Military Frontier">Military Frontier</a> which <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Austria</a> carved out of parts of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_land" title="Crown land">crown lands</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Croatia_in_the_Habsburg_Empire" title="Croatia in the Habsburg Empire">Croatia</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Banovina_of_Slavonia" title="Banovina of Slavonia">Slavonia</a> between 1553–1578 with a view to defending itself against the expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. Many Croats, Serbs and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vlach" title="Vlach">Vlachs</a> immigrated from nearby parts of the Ottoman Empire (Ottoman Bosnia and Serbia) into the region and helped bolster and replenish the population as well as the garrisoned troops in the fight against the Ottomans. The Austrians controlled the Frontier from military headquarters in Vienna and did not make it a <a href="/wiki/Crown_land" title="Crown land">crown land</a>, though it had some special rights in order to encourage settlement in an otherwise deserted, war-ravaged territory. The abolition of military rule took place between 1869 and 1871. In order to attract Serbs to become part of Croatia, on 11 May 1867, the <a href="/wiki/Croatian_Parliament" title="Croatian Parliament">Sabor</a> solemnly declared that "the Triune Kingdom recognizes the Serbian/Vlach people living in it as a nation identical and equal with the Croatian nation". Subsequently, the Military Frontier was incorporated into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Croatia_in_the_Habsburg_Empire" title="Croatia in the Habsburg Empire">Habsburg Croatia</a> in 1881.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Militargrenze,_Wojwodowena_und_Banat.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="312" data-file-width="900" height="76" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Militargrenze%2C_Wojwodowena_und_Banat.jpg/220px-Militargrenze%2C_Wojwodowena_und_Banat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Militargrenze%2C_Wojwodowena_und_Banat.jpg/330px-Militargrenze%2C_Wojwodowena_und_Banat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Militargrenze%2C_Wojwodowena_und_Banat.jpg/440px-Militargrenze%2C_Wojwodowena_und_Banat.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Militargrenze,_Wojwodowena_und_Banat.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the original Krajina, the <a href="/wiki/Military_Frontier" title="Military Frontier">Military Frontier</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> in 1918, the regions formerly forming part of the Military Frontier came under the control of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Yugoslavia</a>, where they formed part of the <a href="/wiki/Sava_Banovina" title="Sava Banovina">Sava Banovina</a>, along with most of the old Croatia-Slavonia. <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">Between the two World Wars</a> the Serbs of the Croatian and Slavonian Krajinas, as well as those of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosnian_Krajina" title="Bosnian Krajina">Bosnian Krajina</a> and of other regions west of <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, organized a notable political party, the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Democratic_Party_(Yugoslavia)" title="Independent Democratic Party (Yugoslavia)">Independent Democratic Party</a> under <a href="/wiki/Svetozar_Pribi%C4%87evi%C4%87" title="Svetozar Pribićević">Svetozar Pribićević</a>. In the new state there existed much tension between the Croats and Serbs over differing political visions, with the campaign for Croatian autonomy culminating in the assassination of a Croatian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leader" title="Leader">leader</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stjepan_Radi%C4%87" title="Stjepan Radić">Stjepan Radić</a>, in the parliament, and repression by the Serb-dominated security structures.</p>
<p>Between 1939 and 1941, in an attempt to resolve the Croat-Serb political and social antagonism in the first Yugoslavia, the kingdom established an autonomous <a href="/wiki/Banovina_of_Croatia" title="Banovina of Croatia">Banovina of Croatia</a> incorporating (amongst other territories) much of the former <a href="/wiki/Military_Frontier" title="Military Frontier">Military Frontier</a> as well as parts of <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>. In 1941 the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a> invaded Yugoslavia and in the aftermath the <a href="/wiki/Independent_State_of_Croatia" title="Independent State of Croatia">Independent State of Croatia</a> (which included whole of today's Bosnia and Herzegovina and parts of Serbia (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Syrmia" title="Eastern Syrmia">Eastern Syrmia</a>) as well) was declared. The Germans installed the <a href="/wiki/Usta%C5%A1e" title="Ustaše">Ustaše</a> (who had allegedly plotted the assassination of the Serbian <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Yugoslavia" title="Alexander I of Yugoslavia">King Alexander I</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> in 1934) as rulers of the new country; the Ustaše authorities promptly pursued a genocidal policy of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Serbs" title="Persecution of Serbs">persecution of Serbs</a>, Jews and Croats (from opposition groups), leading to hundreds of thousands being killed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> During this period, individual Croats coalesced around the ruling authorities or around the communist anti-fascist <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Partisans" title="Yugoslav Partisans">Partisans</a>. Serbs from around the <a href="/wiki/Knin" title="Knin">Knin</a> area tended to join the <a href="/wiki/Chetniks" title="Chetniks">Chetniks</a>, whilst Serbs from the <a href="/wiki/Banovina_(region)" title="Banovina (region)">Banovina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slavonia" title="Slavonia">Slavonia</a> regions tended to join the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Partisans" title="Yugoslav Partisans">Partisans</a>.</p>
<p>At the end of World War II in 1945, the communist-dominated Partisans prevailed and the Krajina region became part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Croatia" title="People's Republic of Croatia">People's Republic of Croatia</a> until 7 April 1963, when the federal republic changed its name to the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Croatia" title="Socialist Republic of Croatia">Socialist Republic of Croatia</a>. <a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Tito</a> suppressed the autonomous political organisations of the region (along with other movements such as the <a href="/wiki/Croatian_Spring" title="Croatian Spring">Croatian Spring</a>); however, the Yugoslav constitutions of 1965 and 1974 did give substantial rights to national minorities - including to the Serbs in SR Croatia.</p>
<p>The Serbian "Krajina" entity to emerge upon Croatia's declaration of independence in 1991 would include three kinds of territories:</p>
<ul>
<li>a large section of the historical Military Frontier, in areas with a majority Serbian population;</li>
<li>areas such as parts of northern Dalmatia, that never formed part of the Frontier but had a majority or a plurality of Serbian population, including the self-proclaimed entity's capital, <a href="/wiki/Knin" title="Knin">Knin</a>;</li>
<li>areas that bordered with Serbia and where Serbs formed a significant minority (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baranja_region" title="Baranja region">Baranja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vukovar" title="Vukovar">Vukovar</a>).</li>
</ul>
<p>Large sections of the historical Military Frontier lay outside of the Republic of Serb Krajina and contained a largely Croat population - these including much of <a href="/wiki/Lika" title="Lika">Lika</a>, the area centred around the city of <a href="/wiki/Bjelovar" title="Bjelovar">Bjelovar</a>, central and south-eastern <a href="/wiki/Slavonia" title="Slavonia">Slavonia</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Creation">Creation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_Serbian_Krajina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Creation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<div class="thumb tright">

</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Republika_srpska_krajina_regije.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="759" data-file-width="1050" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Republika_srpska_krajina_regije.png/200px-Republika_srpska_krajina_regije.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Republika_srpska_krajina_regije.png/300px-Republika_srpska_krajina_regije.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Republika_srpska_krajina_regije.png/400px-Republika_srpska_krajina_regije.png 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Republika_srpska_krajina_regije.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Geographical regions of the Republic of Serbian Krajina</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Serb-populated regions in Croatia were of central concern to the Serbian nationalist movement of the late 1980s, led by <a href="/wiki/Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Slobodan Milošević">Slobodan Milošević</a>. As early as September 1986 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Memorandum_of_the_Serbian_Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts" title="Memorandum of the Serbian Academy of Sciences and Arts">SANU memorandum</a> was published by the Serbian Academy of Arts and Science. It listed a series of Serb nationalists grievances against the Yugoslav federation, claiming that the situation in Kosovo was 'genocide', and complains about alleged discrimination of Serbs at the hands of the Croatian authorities. Among the claims that it makes is that 'except for the time under the <a href="/wiki/Independent_State_of_Croatia" title="Independent State of Croatia">Independent State of Croatia</a>, the Serbs in Croatia have never been as jeopardized as they are today’.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Tension was further fuelled by the overthrow of Vojvodina and Montenegro's government by Milošević's loyalists, and the abrogation of Kosovo's and Vojvodina's autonomy in 1989, which gave Milošević 4 out of 8 votes on the Yugoslav Federal Presidency, thus gaining the power to block every decision made by the Presidency. Furthermore, a series of Serb nationalist rallies held in Croatia during 1989, under pressure from Serbia. For example, on 8 July 1989 a large Serb nationalist rally was held in Knin, and during this rally banners threatening JNA intervention in Croatia, as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chetnik" title="Chetnik">Chetnik</a> iconography were displayed, stunning the Croatian public.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The Croatian pro-independence victory in 1990 made matters more tense, especially since the country's Serbian minority was supported both politically and militarily by the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_People%27s_Army" title="Yugoslav People's Army">Yugoslav People's Army</a>, especially Serbian President Milošević. At the time, Serbs comprised about 12.2% of Croatia's population: 581,663 people declared themselves Serbs in the census of 1991.</p>
<p>Serbs became increasingly opposed to the policies of Franjo Tuđman, elected president of Croatia in April 1990, due to his overt desire for the creation of an independent Croatia. On 30 May 1990, the <a href="/wiki/Serb_Democratic_Party_(Croatia)" title="Serb Democratic Party (Croatia)">Serb Democratic Party</a> of Jovan Rašković broke all ties to the Croatian parliament. The following June in Knin, the Serbs—led by the <a href="/wiki/Serb_Democratic_Party_(Croatia)" title="Serb Democratic Party (Croatia)">Serb Democratic Party</a>—proclaimed the creation of the Association of Municipalities of Northern Dalmatia and Lika. In August 1990, the Serbs began what became known as the <a href="/wiki/Log_Revolution" title="Log Revolution">Log Revolution</a>, where barricades of logs were placed across roads throughout the South as an expression of their secession from Croatia. This effectively cut Croatia in two, separating the coastal region of <a href="/wiki/Dalmatia" title="Dalmatia">Dalmatia</a> from the rest of the country. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Croatia" title="Constitution of Croatia">Croatian constitution</a> was passed in December 1990, which put Serbs in the same category with other ethnic minority groups such as Italians, Hungarians, and others. Some would later justify their claim to an independent Serb state by arguing that the new constitution contradicted the <a href="/wiki/1974_Yugoslav_Constitution" title="1974 Yugoslav Constitution">1974 Yugoslav Constitution</a>, because in their view, Croatia was still legally governed by the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a>, although this ignores the fact that Serbia's constitution, promulgated three months before Croatia's, also contained several provisions violating the 1974 Federal Constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Serbs in Croatia had established a Serbian National Council in July 1990 to coordinate opposition to Croatian independence. Their position was that if Croatia could secede from Yugoslavia, then the Serbs could secede from Croatia. <a href="/wiki/Milan_Babi%C4%87" title="Milan Babić">Milan Babić</a>, a dentist from the southern town of <a href="/wiki/Knin" title="Knin">Knin</a>, was elected president. At his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ICTY" title="ICTY">ICTY</a> trial in 2004, he claimed that "during the events [of 1990–1992], and in particular at the beginning of his political career, he was strongly influenced and misled by Serbian propaganda, which repeatedly referred to the imminent threat of a Croatian genocide perpetrated on the Serbs in Croatia, thus creating an atmosphere of hatred and fear of Croats."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>The rebel Croatian Serbs established a number of <a href="/wiki/Paramilitary" title="Paramilitary">paramilitary</a> militia units under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Milan_Marti%C4%87" title="Milan Martić">Milan Martić</a>, the police chief in Knin.</p>
<p>In August 1990, a referendum was held in Krajina on the question of Serb "sovereignty and autonomy" in Croatia. The resolution was confined exclusively to Serbs so it passed by a majority of 99.7%. As expected, it was declared illegal and invalid by the Croatian government, who stated that Serbs had no constitutional right to break away from Croatian legal territory.</p>
<p>Babić's administration announced the creation of a <a href="/wiki/SAO_Krajina" title="SAO Krajina">Serbian Autonomous Oblast of Krajina</a> (or <i>SAO Krajina</i>) on 21 December 1990. On 16 March 1991 another referendum was held which asked "Are you in favour of the SAO Krajina joining the Republic of Serbia and staying in Yugoslavia with Serbia, Montenegro and others who wish to preserve Yugoslavia?". With 99.8% voting in favour, the referendum was approved and the Krajina assembly declared that "the territory of the SAO Krajina is a constitutive part of the unified state territory of the Republic of Serbia".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> On 1 April 1991, it declared that it would secede from Croatia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTimes-Separation-1Apr1991_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-Separation-1Apr1991-13">[13]</a></sup> Other Serb-dominated communities in eastern Croatia announced that they would also join SAO Krajina and ceased paying taxes to the <a href="/wiki/Zagreb" title="Zagreb">Zagreb</a> government, and began implementing its own currency system, army regiments, and postal service.</p>
<p>Croatia held a <a href="/wiki/Croatian_independence_referendum,_1991" title="Croatian independence referendum, 1991">referendum on independence on 19 May 1991</a>, in which the electorate—minus many Serbs, who chose to boycott it—voted overwhelmingly for independence with the option of confederate union with other Yugoslav states. On 25 June 1991, Croatia and Slovenia both declared their independence from Yugoslavia. As the JNA attempted unsuccessfully to suppress Slovenia's independence in the short <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slovenian_War" title="Slovenian War">Slovenian War</a>, clashes between rebelled Croatian Serbs and Croatian security forces broke out almost immediately, leaving dozens dead on both sides. Serbs calling themselves <a href="/wiki/Chetniks" title="Chetniks">Chetniks</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Seselj_article_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Seselj_article-14">[14]</a></sup> were supported by the remnants of the JNA (whose members were now only from Serbia and Montenegro), which provided them military arms. Many Croatians fled their homes in fear, or were forced out by the rebel Serbs. The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> attempted to broker ceasefires and peace settlements, but all to no avail.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Demographics_of_RSK.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="519" data-file-width="828" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Demographics_of_RSK.jpg/280px-Demographics_of_RSK.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Demographics_of_RSK.jpg/420px-Demographics_of_RSK.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Demographics_of_RSK.jpg/560px-Demographics_of_RSK.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Demographics_of_RSK.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Change in the ethnic composition of Krajina from April 1991 to July 1992. Serbs increased from 52.3% to 88% of the total population</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:War_Flag_of_Serbian_Krajina.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/War_Flag_of_Serbian_Krajina.svg/250px-War_Flag_of_Serbian_Krajina.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/War_Flag_of_Serbian_Krajina.svg/375px-War_Flag_of_Serbian_Krajina.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/War_Flag_of_Serbian_Krajina.svg/500px-War_Flag_of_Serbian_Krajina.svg.png 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:War_Flag_of_Serbian_Krajina.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
War Flag of Serbian Krajina</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Around August 1991, the leadership of the Serbian Krajina, and that of Serbia, allegedly agreed to embark on a campaign which the ICTY prosecutors described as a "joint criminal enterprise" whose purpose "was the forcible removal of the majority of the Croat and other non-Serb population from approximately one-third of the territory of the Republic of Croatia, an area he planned to become part of a new Serb-dominated state."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The leaders are documented to have included Milan Babić, and other rebelled Croatian Serbs' figures such as Milan Martić, the Serbian militia leader <a href="/wiki/Vojislav_%C5%A0e%C5%A1elj" title="Vojislav Šešelj">Vojislav Šešelj</a> and Yugoslav Army commanders including General <a href="/wiki/Ratko_Mladi%C4%87" title="Ratko Mladić">Ratko Mladić</a>, who was at the time the commander of JNA forces in Croatia.</p>
<p>According to testimony given by Babić in his subsequent war crimes trial, during the summer of 1991 the Serbian secret police—under Milošević's command—set up "a parallel structure of state security and the police of Krajina and units commanded by the state security of Serbia".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Shadowy groups of paramilitaries with names such as the "Vukovi sa Vucjaka" ("Wolves from Vucjak") and the "Beli Orlovi" ("White Eagles"), funded by the Serbian <a href="/wiki/Secret_police" title="Secret police">secret police</a>, were also a key component of this structure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Seselj_indictment_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Seselj_indictment-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>A wider-scale war was launched in August 1991. Over the following months, a large area of territory, amounting to a third of Croatia, was controlled by the rebel Serbs. The Croatian population suffered heavily, fleeing or evicted with numerous killings, leading to <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnic cleansing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY_evidence_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-ICTY_evidence-18">[18]</a></sup> The bulk of the fighting occurred between August and December 1991 when approximately 80,000 Croats were expelled (and some were killed).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Croatian_refugees_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Croatian_refugees-19">[19]</a></sup> Many more died and or were displaced in fighting in eastern <a href="/wiki/Slavonia" title="Slavonia">Slavonia</a> (this territory along the Croatian/Serbian border was not part of the Krajina, and it was the JNA that was the principal actor in that part of the conflict). The total number of exiled Croats and other non-Serbs range from 170,000 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ICTY" title="ICTY">ICTY</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> up to a quarter of a million people (<a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the latter half of 1991, Croatia was beginning to form an army and their main defenders, the local police, were overpowered by the JNA military who supported rebelled Croatian Serbs. The RSK was located entirely inland, but they soon started advancing deeper into Croatian territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY_evidence_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-ICTY_evidence-18">[18]</a></sup> Among other places, they shelled the Croatian coastal town of <a href="/wiki/Zadar" title="Zadar">Zadar</a> killing over 80 people in nearby areas and damaging the <a href="/wiki/Maslenica_Bridge_(D8)" title="Maslenica Bridge (D8)">Maslenica Bridge</a> that connected northern and southern Croatia, in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Coast-91" title="Operation Coast-91">Operation Coast-91</a>. They also tried to overtake <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0ibenik" title="Šibenik">Šibenik</a>, but the defenders successfully repelled the attack by JNA, in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_%C5%A0ibenik_(1991)" title="Battle of Šibenik (1991)">Battle of Šibenik</a>. The main city theatre was also bombed by JNA forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sibenik_theatre_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sibenik_theatre-22">[22]</a></sup> The city of <a href="/wiki/Vukovar" title="Vukovar">Vukovar</a>, however, was completely devastated by JNA attacks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tanner:_Croatia_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tanner:_Croatia-23">[23]</a></sup> The city of Vukovar that warded off JNA attacks for months eventually fell, ending the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vukovar" title="Battle of Vukovar">Battle of Vukovar</a>. 2,000 defenders of Vukovar and civilians were killed, 800 went missing and 22,000 were forced into exile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The wounded were taken from Vukovar Hospital to Ovcara near Vukovar where they were executed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Formal_proclamations">Formal proclamations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_Serbian_Krajina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Formal proclamations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On 19 December 1991, the SAO Krajina proclaimed itself the Republic of Serbian Krajina. The Constitution of Serbian Krajina came into effect the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> On 26 February 1992, the SAO Western Slavonia and SAO Slavonia, Baranja and Western Srem were added to the RSK, which initially had only encompassed the territories within the SAO Krajina. The Serb Army of Krajina (<i>Српска Војска Крајине</i> / <i>Srpska Vojska Krajine</i> ; abbreviated <i>СВК</i> / <i>SVK</i>) (or the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Serbian_Krajina_Army" title="Republic of Serbian Krajina Army">Republic of Serbian Krajina Army</a>) was officially formed on 19 March 1992. The RSK occupied an area of some 17,028 km² at its greatest extent.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="1992_ceasefire">1992 ceasefire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_Serbian_Krajina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1992 ceasefire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_war_in_Yugoslavia,_1993.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1242" data-file-width="1887" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Map_of_war_in_Yugoslavia%2C_1993.png/300px-Map_of_war_in_Yugoslavia%2C_1993.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Map_of_war_in_Yugoslavia%2C_1993.png/450px-Map_of_war_in_Yugoslavia%2C_1993.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Map_of_war_in_Yugoslavia%2C_1993.png/600px-Map_of_war_in_Yugoslavia%2C_1993.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_war_in_Yugoslavia,_1993.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
War in former Yugoslavia, 1993</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Under the <a href="/wiki/Vance_plan" title="Vance plan">Vance plan</a>, signed in November 1991, Presidents Tuđman and Milošević agreed to a United Nations peace plan put forward by <a href="/wiki/Cyrus_Vance" title="Cyrus Vance">Cyrus Vance</a>. A final ceasefire agreement, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sarajevo_Agreement" title="Sarajevo Agreement">Sarajevo Agreement</a>, was signed by representatives of the two sides in January 1992, paving the way for the implementation of the Vance plan. Four United Nations Protected Areas (UNPAs) were established in Croatian territory which was claimed by RSK, and the plan called for the withdrawal of the JNA from Croatia and for the return of refugees to their homes in the UNPAs.</p>
<p>The JNA officially withdrew from Croatia in May 1992 but much of its weaponry and many of its personnel remained in the Serb-held areas and were turned over to the RSK's security forces. Refugees were not allowed to return to their homes and many of the remaining Croats and other nationalities left in the RSK were expelled or killed in the following months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tanner:_Croatia_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tanner:_Croatia-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Babic_Guilty_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Babic_Guilty-28">[28]</a></sup> On 21 February 1992, the creation of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Protection_Force" title="United Nations Protection Force">United Nations Protection Force</a> (UNPROFOR) was authorised by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council" title="UN Security Council">UN Security Council</a> for an initial period of a year, to provide security to the UNPAs.</p>
<p>The agreement effectively froze the front lines for the next three years. Croatia and the RSK had effectively fought each other to a standstill. The Republic of Serbian Krajina was not recognised <a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a> by any other country or international organisation. Nevertheless, it gained support from Serbia's allies, like <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="After_the_ceasefire">After the ceasefire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_Serbian_Krajina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: After the ceasefire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>UNPROFOR was deployed throughout the region to maintain the ceasefire, although in practice its light armament and restricted rules of engagement meant that it was little more than an observer force. It proved wholly unable to ensure that refugees returned to the RSK. Indeed, the rebel Croatian Serb authorities continued to make efforts to ensure that they could <i>never</i> return, destroying villages and cultural and religious monuments to erase the previous existence of the Croatian inhabitants of the Krajina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tanner:_Croatia_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-Tanner:_Croatia-23">[23]</a></sup> Milan Babić later testified that this policy was driven from Belgrade through the Serbian secret police—and ultimately Milošević—who he claimed were in control of all the administrative institutions and armed forces in the Krajina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Babic_testification_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Babic_testification-29">[29]</a></sup> This would certainly explain why the Yugoslav National Army took the side of the rebelled Croatian Serbs in spite of its claims to be acting as a "peacekeeping" force. Milošević denied this, claiming that Babić had made it up "out of fear".</p>
<p>The Army of Serbian Krajina frequently attacked neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Biha%C4%87" title="Bihać">Bihać</a> enclave (then in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Republic of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Republic of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>) with heavy artillery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kotar_Glina_i_Knin.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2128" data-file-width="2184" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Kotar_Glina_i_Knin.jpg/220px-Kotar_Glina_i_Knin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Kotar_Glina_i_Knin.jpg/330px-Kotar_Glina_i_Knin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Kotar_Glina_i_Knin.jpg/440px-Kotar_Glina_i_Knin.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kotar_Glina_i_Knin.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Two Autonomous Districts of Croatia are shown in dark green.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With the creation of new <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Croatia" title="Counties of Croatia">Croatian counties</a> on 30 December 1992, the Croatian government also set aside two autonomous regions (<i>kotar</i>) for ethnic Serbs in the areas of Krajina:</p>
<ul>
<li>Autonomous District of Glina (<a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">Croatian</a>: <span lang="hr" xml:lang="hr"><i>Autonomni kotar Glina</i></span>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbian_Cyrillic_language" title="Serbian Cyrillic language">Serbian Cyrillic</a>: <span lang="sr" xml:lang="sr"><span class="Unicode">Аутономни котар Глина</span></span>)
<ul>
<li>Municipalities <i><a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a></i> within the Autonomous District of Glina were <a href="/wiki/Glina,_Croatia" title="Glina, Croatia">Glina</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vrginmost" title="Vrginmost">Vrginmost</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hrvatska_Kostajnica" title="Hrvatska Kostajnica">Hrvatska Kostajnica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dvor,_Croatia" title="Dvor, Croatia">Dvor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vojni%C4%87" title="Vojnić">Vojnić</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Autonomous District of Knin (<a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">Croatian</a>: <span lang="hr" xml:lang="hr"><i>Autonomni kotar Knin</i></span>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbian_Cyrillic_language" title="Serbian Cyrillic language">Serbian Cyrillic</a>: <span lang="sr" xml:lang="sr"><span class="Unicode">Аутономни котар Книн</span></span>)</li>
</ul>
<p>However, Serbs considered this too late, as it was not the amount of autonomy they wanted, and by now they had declared <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a> independence.</p>
<p>The districts never actually functioned since they were located within the self-proclaimed Republic of Serbian Krajina. Existence of the Autonomous District of Glina was also provided in the draft of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Z-4_plan" title="Z-4 plan">Z-4 plan</a>, that was rejected. After <a href="/wiki/Operation_Storm" title="Operation Storm">Operation Storm</a>, the application of the law which allowed autonomy would be temporarily suspended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> In 2000 this part of the law was formally repealed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Decline">Decline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_Serbian_Krajina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Decline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Goran_Hadzic_1992_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1065" data-file-width="846" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Goran_Hadzic_1992_2.jpg/150px-Goran_Hadzic_1992_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Goran_Hadzic_1992_2.jpg/225px-Goran_Hadzic_1992_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Goran_Hadzic_1992_2.jpg/300px-Goran_Hadzic_1992_2.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Goran_Hadzic_1992_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1992: RSK president <a href="/wiki/Goran_Had%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Goran Hadžić">Goran Hadžić</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The partial implementation of the Vance Plan drove a wedge between the governments of the RSK and Serbia, the RSK's principal backer and supplier of fuel, arms and money. Milan Babić strongly opposed the Vance Plan but was overruled by the RSK's assembly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tanner:_Croatia_23-3"><a href="#cite_note-Tanner:_Croatia-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 26 February 1992, Babić was deposed and replaced as President of the RSK by <a href="/wiki/Goran_Had%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Goran Hadžić">Goran Hadžić</a>, a Milošević loyalist. Babić remained involved in RSK politics but as a considerably weaker figure.</p>
<p>The position of the RSK eroded steadily over the following three years. On the surface, the RSK had all the trappings of a state: army, parliament, president, government and ministries, currency and stamps. However its economy was wholly dependent on support from the rump Yugoslavia, which had the effect of importing that country's <a href="/wiki/Hyperinflation" title="Hyperinflation">hyperinflation</a>.</p>
<p>The economic situation soon became disastrous. By 1994, only 36,000 of the RSK's 430,000 citizens were employed. The war had severed the RSK's trade links with the rest of Croatia, leaving its few industries idle. With few natural resources of its own it had to import most of the goods and fuel it required. Agriculture was devastated, and operated at little more than a subsistence level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-svarm_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-svarm-4">[4]</a></sup> Professionals went to Serbia or elsewhere to escape the republic's economic hardships. To make matters worse, the RSK's government was grossly corrupt and the region became a haven for black marketeering and other criminal activity. It was clear by the mid-1990s that without a peace deal or support from Yugoslavia the RSK was not economically viable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Evidence_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Evidence-34">[34]</a></sup> This was especially evident in Belgrade, where the RSK had become an unwanted economic and political burden for Milošević. Much to his frustration, the rebel Croatian Serbs rebuffed his government's demands to settle the conflict.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tanner:_Croatia_23-4"><a href="#cite_note-Tanner:_Croatia-23">[23]</a></sup> In July 1992 the RSK issued its own currency, the <a href="/wiki/Krajina_dinar" title="Krajina dinar">Krajina dinar</a> (HRKR), in parallel with the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_dinar" title="Yugoslav dinar">Yugoslav dinar</a>. This was followed by the "October dinar" (HRKO), first issued on 1 October 1993 and equal to 1,000,000 Reformed Dinar, and the "1994 dinar", first issued on 1 January 1994, and equal to 1,000,000,000 October dinar. The RSK's weakness also adversely affected its armed forces, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vojska_Srpske_Krajine" title="Vojska Srpske Krajine">Vojska Srpske Krajine</a> (VSK). Since the 1992 ceasefire agreement, Croatia had spent heavily on importing weapons and training its armed forces with assistance from American contractors. In contrast, the VSK had grown steadily weaker, with its soldiers poorly motivated, trained and equipped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tanner:_Croatia_23-5"><a href="#cite_note-Tanner:_Croatia-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-National_Security_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-National_Security-35">[35]</a></sup> There were only about 55,000 of them to cover a front of some 600 km in Croatia plus 100 km along the border with the <a href="/wiki/Biha%C4%87" title="Bihać">Bihać</a> pocket in Bosnia. With 16,000 stationed in eastern Slavonia, only about 39,000 were left to defend the main part of the RSK. Overall, only 30,000 were capable of full mobilization, yet they faced a far stronger Croatian army. Also, political divisions between Hadžić and Babić occasionally led to physical and sometimes even armed confrontations between their supporters; Babić himself was assaulted and beaten in an incident in <a href="/wiki/Benkovac" title="Benkovac">Benkovac</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dokumenti_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dokumenti-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 1993 the revitalized Croatian army attacked the Serbian positions around <a href="/wiki/Maslenica" title="Maslenica">Maslenica</a> in southern Croatia which curtailed their access to the sea via <a href="/wiki/Novigrad,_Zadar_County" title="Novigrad, Zadar County">Novigrad</a>.</p>
<p>In mid-1993, the RSK authorities started a campaign to formally create a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Serbian_Republic" title="United Serbian Republic">United Serbian Republic</a>.</p>
<p>In a second offensive in September 1993 the Croatian army overran the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medak_pocket" title="Medak pocket">Medak pocket</a> in the southern Krajina in a push to regain Serb-held Croatian territory. This action was halted by international diplomacy but although the rebel Croatian Serbs brought reinforcements forward fairly quickly, the strength of the Croatian forces proved superior. Hadžić sent an urgent request to Belgrade for reinforcements, arms and equipment. In response, around 4,000 paramilitaries under the command of <a href="/wiki/Vojislav_%C5%A0e%C5%A1elj" title="Vojislav Šešelj">Vojislav Šešelj</a> (the <a href="/wiki/White_Eagles_(paramilitary)" title="White Eagles (paramilitary)">White Eagles</a>) and "<a href="/wiki/Arkan" title="Arkan">Arkan</a>" (the <a href="/wiki/Serb_Volunteer_Guard" title="Serb Volunteer Guard">Serb Volunteer Guard</a>) arrived to bolster the VSK.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operation_Storm">Operation Storm</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_Serbian_Krajina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Operation Storm">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Operation_Flash" title="Operation Flash">Operation Flash</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Storm" title="Operation Storm">Operation Storm</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Martic-order1995.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3507" data-file-width="2472" height="312" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Martic-order1995.jpg/220px-Martic-order1995.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Martic-order1995.jpg/330px-Martic-order1995.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Martic-order1995.jpg/440px-Martic-order1995.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Martic-order1995.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The order to evacuate ethnic Serbs from RSK territory, issued by the Krajina Defence Council and signed by <a href="/wiki/Milan_Marti%C4%87" title="Milan Martić">Milan Martić</a>; 4 August 1995</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the rejection by both sides of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Z-4_plan" title="Z-4 plan">Z-4 plan</a> for reintegration, the RSK's end came in 1995, when Croatian forces gained control of <a href="/wiki/SAO_Western_Slavonia" title="SAO Western Slavonia">SAO Western Slavonia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Flash" title="Operation Flash">Operation Flash</a> (May) followed by the biggest part of occupied Croatia in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Storm" title="Operation Storm">Operation Storm</a> (August). The Krajina Serb Supreme Defence Council met under president <a href="/wiki/Milan_Marti%C4%87" title="Milan Martić">Milan Martić</a> to discuss the situation. A decision was reached at 16:45 to "start evacuating the population unfit for military service from the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Knin" title="Knin">Knin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benkovac" title="Benkovac">Benkovac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Obrovac,_Croatia" title="Obrovac, Croatia">Obrovac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drni%C5%A1" title="Drniš">Drniš</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gra%C4%8Dac" title="Gračac">Gračac</a>." The RSK was disbanded and most of its Serb population (from 150,000 to 200,000 people) fled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tanner:_Croatia_23-6"><a href="#cite_note-Tanner:_Croatia-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amnesty_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty-38">[38]</a></sup> Only 5,000 to 6,000 people remained, mostly the elderly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goldstein_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-goldstein-39">[39]</a></sup> Croatian historian <a href="/wiki/Ivo_Goldstein" title="Ivo Goldstein">Ivo Goldstein</a> wrote, "<i>The reasons for the Serb exodus are complex. Some had to leave because the Serb army had forced them to, while others feared the revenge of the Croatian army or of their former Croat neighbours, whom they had driven away and whose homes they had mostly looted (and it was later shown that this fear was far from groundless).</i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goldstein_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-goldstein-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most of the refugees ended up in Serbia, Bosnia and eastern Slavonia. Some of those who remained were murdered, tortured and forcibly expelled by the Croatian Army and police.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amnesty_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between 2001 and 2012, the ICTY had prosecuted Croatian generals <a href="/wiki/Ante_Gotovina" title="Ante Gotovina">Ante Gotovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mladen_Marka%C4%8D" title="Mladen Markač">Mladen Markač</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ivan_%C4%8Cermak" title="Ivan Čermak">Ivan Čermak</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Trial_of_Gotovina_et_al" title="Trial of Gotovina et al">Trial of Gotovina et al</a> for their involvement in crimes committed during and in the aftermath of Operation Storm. The indictment and the subsequent trial on charges of crimes against humanity and violations of the laws or customs of war described several killings, widespread arson and looting committed by Croatian soldiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gotovina_indictment_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gotovina_indictment-40">[40]</a></sup> In April 2011, Gotovina and Markač were convicted to prison sentences, while Čermak was acquitted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gotovina_indictment_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gotovina_indictment-40">[40]</a></sup> Gotovina and Markač appealed the verdict and in November 2012 the Appeals Chamber of the ICTY overturned their convictions, acquitting them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABC_News_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_News-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_events">Later events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_Serbian_Krajina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Later events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hrvatsko_Podunavlje.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1204" data-file-width="881" height="301" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Hrvatsko_Podunavlje.png/220px-Hrvatsko_Podunavlje.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Hrvatsko_Podunavlje.png/330px-Hrvatsko_Podunavlje.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Hrvatsko_Podunavlje.png/440px-Hrvatsko_Podunavlje.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hrvatsko_Podunavlje.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the remaining Krajina territory in eastern Croatia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The parts of the former RSK in eastern Croatia (along the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a>) remained in place, in what was previously the <a href="/wiki/SAO_Eastern_Slavonia,_Baranja_and_Western_Syrmia" title="SAO Eastern Slavonia, Baranja and Western Syrmia">SAO Eastern Slavonia, Baranja and Western Syrmia</a>.</p>
<p>In 1995, Milan Milanović, formerly a Republic of Serbian Krajina official, signed the <a href="/wiki/Erdut_Agreement" title="Erdut Agreement">Erdut Agreement</a> as a representative of the Serbian side. This agreement, co-signed by the representative of the Croatian Government, was sponsored by the United Nations, and it set up a transitional period during which the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Transitional_Authority_for_Eastern_Slavonia,_Baranja_and_Western_Sirmium" title="United Nations Transitional Authority for Eastern Slavonia, Baranja and Western Sirmium">United Nations Transitional Authority for Eastern Slavonia, Baranja and Western Sirmium</a> (UNTAES) peacekeeping mission would oversee a peaceful reintegration of this territory into Croatia, starting on 15 January 1996. In 1998, the UNTAES mission was complete and the territory was formally returned to Croatia. Based on the Erdut Agreement, the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Council_of_Municipalities" title="Joint Council of Municipalities">Joint Council of Municipalities</a> was established in the region in 1997.</p>
<p>After the peaceful reintegration, two Croatian islands on the Danube, the <a href="/wiki/Island_of_%C5%A0arengrad" title="Island of Šarengrad">Island of Šarengrad</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Island_of_Vukovar" title="Island of Vukovar">Island of Vukovar</a>, remained under Serbian military control. In 2004, Serbian military was withdrawn from the islands and replaced with Serbian police. The islands remain an open question as the Croatian side insists on applying <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Badinter_Arbitration_Committee" title="Badinter Arbitration Committee">Badinter Arbitration Committee</a> decisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1995 a Croatian court sentenced former RSK president <a href="/wiki/Goran_Had%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Goran Hadžić">Goran Hadžić</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Trial_in_absentia" title="Trial in absentia">in absentia</a></i> to 20 years in prison for rocket attacks on <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0ibenik" title="Šibenik">Šibenik</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vodice,_Croatia" title="Vodice, Croatia">Vodice</a>. In 1999 he was sentenced to an additional 20 years for war crimes in <a href="/wiki/Tenja" title="Tenja">Tenja</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Osijek" title="Osijek">Osijek</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rferl-hr-2011_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-rferl-hr-2011-43">[43]</a></sup> and in 2002 Croatia's state attorney brought another indictment against him for the murder of almost 1,300 Croats in Vukovar, Osijek, Vinkovci, <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDupanja" title="Županja">Županja</a> and elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rferl-hr-2011_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-rferl-hr-2011-43">[43]</a></sup> On 4 June 2004, the ICTY indicted him on 14 counts of war crimes and <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In 2011 he was arrested and extradited to the Hague, where his initial trial hearing was held on 25 July the same year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_Serbian_Krajina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>According to the indictment of prosecutor <a href="/wiki/Carla_Del_Ponte" title="Carla Del Ponte">Carla Del Ponte</a> against <a href="/wiki/Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Slobodan Milošević">Slobodan Milošević</a> at the ICTY, the Croat and non-Serb population from the 1991 census was approximately as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center; width:80%;">
<tr>
<th>Census (1991)</th>

<th class="background: red; color: white"><a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croats</a></th>
<th class="background: red; color: white">Others</th>
<th class="background: red; color: white">Total</th>
</tr>

</tr>
</table>
<p>Thus Serbs comprised 52.3% and Croats 35.8% of the population of SAO Krajina respectively in 1991.</p>
<p>According to data set forth at the meeting of the Government of the RSK in July 1992, its ethnic composition was 88% Serbs, 7% Croats, 5% others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dokumenti_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dokumenti-36">[36]</a></sup> As of November 1993, less than 400 ethnic Croats still resided in UNPA Sector South,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> and between 1,500 and 2,000 remained in UNPA Sector North.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNCHR_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNCHR-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Towns">Towns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_Serbian_Krajina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Towns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_status">Legal status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_Serbian_Krajina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Legal status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Takozvana_Republika_Srpska_Krajina.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Takozvana_Republika_Srpska_Krajina.JPG/220px-Takozvana_Republika_Srpska_Krajina.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Takozvana_Republika_Srpska_Krajina.JPG/330px-Takozvana_Republika_Srpska_Krajina.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Takozvana_Republika_Srpska_Krajina.JPG/440px-Takozvana_Republika_Srpska_Krajina.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Takozvana_Republika_Srpska_Krajina.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Republic of Serbian Krajina documents</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During its existence, this entity did not achieve international recognition. On 29 November 1991, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Badinter_commission" title="Badinter commission">Badinter commission</a> concluded that Yugoslavia was "in dissolution" and that the republics – including Croatia – should be recognized as independent states when they asked so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> They also assigned these republics territorial integrity. For most of the world this was a reason to recognize Croatia. However, Serbia did not accept the conclusions of the commission in that period and recognized Croatia only after Croatian military actions (Oluja and Bljesak) and the Dayton agreement.</p>
<p>On 20 November 1991 <a href="/wiki/Peter_Carington,_6th_Baron_Carrington" title="Peter Carington, 6th Baron Carrington">Lord Carrington</a> asked <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Badinter_commission" title="Badinter commission">Badinter commission</a>: "Does the <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbian</a> population in <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, as one of the constituent peoples of Yugoslavia, have the right to <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">self-determination</a>?" The commission concluded on 11 January 1992 "that the Serbian population in Bosnia and Herzegovina and Croatia is entitled to all the rights concerned to <a href="/wiki/Minority_group" title="Minority group">minorities</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic groups</a>[...]" and "that the Republics must afford the members of those minorities and ethnic groups all the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_right" title="Human right">human rights</a> and fundamental <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedom_(political)" title="Freedom (political)">freedoms</a> recognized in <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a>, including, where appropriate, the right to choose their <a href="/wiki/Nationality" title="Nationality">nationality</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_in_exile">Government in exile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_Serbian_Krajina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Government in exile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_Serbian_Krajina&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(January 2013)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>There exists a self-proclaimed <a href="/wiki/Government_in_exile" title="Government in exile">government in exile</a> for the Republic of Serbian Krajina. This government existed for a short time period after Operation Storm, but was reconstituted in 2005. This self-proclaimed government has changed the official name of the Republic of Serbian Krajina to Republic of Serb-Krajina. At the Belgrade meeting, the former legislators declared themselves to be the legitimate continuation of the RSK government and called for the re-creation of the RSK on the basis of the 1994 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Z-4_plan" title="Z-4 plan">Z-4 plan</a>, which had called for Krajina to have a status of "more than <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/autonomy" title="wiktionary:autonomy">autonomy</a>, less than independence" within <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-b92-dokumenti-z-4-plan_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-b92-dokumenti-z-4-plan-52">[52]</a></sup> They announced that a parliamentary election would be held and that the new name of the self-proclaimed state would be "Republic of Serb-Krajina". The meeting elected <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Milorad_Buha&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Milorad Buha (page does not exist)">Milorad Buha</a>, member of the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Radical_Party" title="Serbian Radical Party">Serbian Radical Party</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Prime_minister" title="Prime minister">prime minister</a> as well as six ministers without portfolio whose names were not revealed.</p>
<p>This move was criticized by many, including top <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatian</a> government officials, as well as senior representatives of Serbs in Croatia. They all stated that such a meeting would harm Serb-Croat reconciliation and relations between the communities in <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>. It was pointed out that the Krajina Serb legislators had rejected the Z-4 proposal when it had originally been put forward. Some Serbian nationalists also criticized the move, saying that a government in exile should have been created as soon as possible after Operation Storm, not 10 years later.</p>
